  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Elden Ring is simply an outstanding game which  represents a remarkable accomplishment in the realm of open-world gaming, skillfully merging FromSoftware's intense combat mechanics with awe-inspiring exploration. The expansive and stunning world is brimming with hidden mysteries waiting to be uncovered, while the diverse character customization options provide players with unparalleled freedom. The challenging boss fights deliver a thrilling and demanding experience, establishing its status as one of the finest action RPGs to date. 

Nevertheless, some may find the difficulty progression to be lacking, as the only strong areas are the optional ones which present a greater challenge compared to the main storyline. Despite this minor setback, Elden Ring is a must-have for enthusiasts of immersive journeys and intricate world design.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Mar 11, 2024
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>This is best game I have ever played. For context, if there is an easy. mode, I will absolutely take it, so learning how to overcome this game (and platinum it) was a new and rewarding experience for me. I loved the process: I had to get stuck, pivot, research, explore and ultimately get better. Then I could take on that boss who was so terrifying before. Its so satisfying discovering the right strat for you. Visually and narratively, I found it imaginative and immersive. I loved that the tree would subconsciously guide you to where you need to go. I felt like the characters would just give you enough to go on to peak your curiosity about their quest lines although saying this, I don’t know how I could have completed all of them without guides. I don’t think thats a bad thing, I love doing the research and it’s been fun to watch how other players solve the various narrative puzzles. I really loved the fact that I didn't feel like the game designers weren’t telling me exactly what to do, how to behave and what to think - like so many games nowadays do. I find that to be so patronising and just…yucky… so for me I didn’t feel like they were inserting themselves or their political messages into my time of escapism. So hiphiphooray for that! I love that every NG+ presents itself with a new opportunity to experience the game differently- a new strat, a new build, a respec, more items to find, a different ending to aim for. I haven’t even spent much time in multiplayer, so that’s something I want lto try next, but only after Sekiro! Overall, it’s a rewarding a high quality gaming experience. Thanks Miyazaki and team for all the hard work and love put into it!</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>After over 100 hours of gameplay and a platinum trophy, I'd say this is an excellent game, though not quite as legendary as some of From's own previous titles. However, this is the most accessible and simply fun game From Software has made. There is more variety is weapons/items than ever, and it is easier than Bloodborne/Sekiro/Dark Souls that came before. I truly don't understand the difficulty complaints. The game is hardest at the beginning, but gets progressively easier as you continue. I probably died about 10 times in my first playthrough, and I'd say I'm about average skill level. Elden RIng gives you more opportunity to overcome challenges through clever use of the tools available to you than any previous From Software game. There are creative damage buffs, spirit ashes, enemy weaknesses, etc. The game is easy after you get the mimic spirit ash. If you're feeling overwhelmed by an area, you probably need to go somewhere else first that will be easier. Last thing I'll say is that this game is a lot more enjoyable if you try to relax and avoid a completionist mindset, which can be exhausting given the open-world structure.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

There is no pause button, the game will keep going even if you are in a menu screen. 2. Odd reason but there are too many bosses and too many repetitive bosses. 3. The soundtrack is actually pretty mediocre. 4. The story is convoluted and honestly just dumb. 5. The voice acting is bad. 6. The graphics are alright but this game looks and feels like a slow PC game, not a game that you would play on a console. 7. This game is artificially hard in a lot of ways. By that, I mean that you're character is slow and almost every enemy is much faster than you. Another way this game is artificially hard is that certain enemies are allowed to harm you through barriers and walls (glitches that are purposely left in). 8. This game is chore to play. 9.   </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>The Good
1. Exploration and discovery that's driven entirely by the player.
2. Stunning world design that blends a new open-world with the classic enclosed Soulsborne-style locations.
3. Challenging combat that is both rewarding and thrilling.
4. A visually stunning world that is diverse and memorable.
5. A compelling, layered, and multi-faceted story that demands to be analyzed and unpacked.

The Bad
1. Still, at its core, a difficult game designed for a specific kind of person with little in the way of approachability options.
2. Online multiplayer still requires jumping through hoops.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Overall score : 8.9/10

Elden Ring was an amazing game,yet not a masterpiece as many people claimed,but still **** world was fantastic,easily my favourite open world in any game and the scenery was breath taking There were numerous different and interesting areas  to travel to.Exploration felt great and the npc questlines were pretty good as well.

Now let's talk about the **** first I considered them fine ,I wasnt the biggest fan of them,but they were cool.That kinda changed as I was getting closer the end of the game ,as many MANY bosses were being reused ,even main ones and in the end only 9 bosses proved to be truly unique.

Moving on to another problem ,which is the lategame .I've noticed that the lategame is balanced around meta builds(which can turn the game piss easy) and for me who didnt use one it was kinda harsh ,but I managed.I really think they went kinda overboard with the fights close at the end .Also I was not a fan of the end basically being a boss rush.Nonetheless I really liked some of these fights ,such as maliketh ,radagon ,melania and mohg.This review makes it seem like I dont like the game ,but that's not true,cause it's probably my 10th fav ,I'm just doing a fair critique on it.

To sum things up Elden ring is an amazing experience and non souls fans can get into it more easily compared to otheer souls. i definitely recommend it.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Too hard.

It's just not fun. And although they have introduced things like summons to make gameplay easier, unless you got like a lot of MP to summon a bunch at a time, it doesn't help much for specific enemies, or at least certain kinds of summons. And I don't want this game to just become a quest for finding a bunch of summons and grinding to get more MP, just because the game is just too hard.

I don't get how people enjoy such a game, dying so often. Some claim that after winning against a boss after having died to it multiple times feels satisfying. For me, a lot of times when I get to this point, I just feel like I've wasted so much time.

To be honest, maybe it's just because I **** at these kind of games. I tried liking it, the lore looks very interesting, the enemy design and building designs look often very cool to me, and the world design in general also looks pretty good to me.

But it's just so frustrating dying so very often. If I make progress than it's just very slow until I eventually hit a road block like a boss, which makes it very frustrating for me to continue.

I don't like the game at all, but I can see how others like it. As for me, I won't be finishing it anytime soon.

This being the case I rate this game poorly, but that's probably also because this is not my type of game. I'm not good enough as a gamer to play a Souls game.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

    Nagatsu11
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Mar 17, 2023
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Let me preface this with the fact that I (typically) do not like Souls-like games. I find the typical formula to be too tediously difficult with no way to break the tedium due to the relatively closed in spaces and linear nature of their previous titles.

Elden Ring seems to be the antithesis of this philosophy. Almost from startup you have access to most of an ENORMOUS open world with only subtle hints of where you /should/ go - but even for people who prefer a clear direction because exploration is extremely well rewarded with new gear, more levels, stunning vistas, etc.

True to FromSoft form, this game IS hard - but with the freedom to leave and come back stronger it doesn't feel as tedious or insurmountable as other Souls-like. With previous titles you had to Git Gud to progress, but with Elden Ring, Gitting Gud feels like a natural consequence of simply playing the game. Even if a boss feels impossible (looking at you Maliketh), there are SO many tools at your disposal to eventually overcome it. An amazingly helpful community ready and willing to help overcome any hurdle that proves too high (or if you are looking for a specific piece of gear; patchesemporium &amp; beyondthefog on reddit), summons, and -to my surprise and delight- a simple change of tactics/weapons all prove startling effective. Over 700 hours in across 2 platforms (steam &amp; ps4) and I can very easily see pouring in another 700+; and not regret a single moment. I cannot recommend this game enough. Even if you don't like Souls-like, give this one a chance.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">
        Read More
      </span> <!----> <!----></button></div> <!----></div></div> <div class="c-siteReview_extra u-grid u-grid-gap-medium g-inner-spacing-medium o-border-thin-top g-border-gray30 c-siteReview_extra-user"><!----> <div class="c-siteReview_externalLink g-color-gray80 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter c-siteReview_flag"><svg class="g-outer-spacing-right-small"><use xlink:href="#flag"></use></svg> <span class="g-text-link u-text-underline-under u-text-uppercase">Report</span></div> <!----> <div class="c-siteReview_platform g-text-bold g-color-gray80 g-text-xsmall u-text-right u-text-uppercase">
      PlayStation 4
    </div></div></div> <!----> <!----></div><div><div class="c-siteReview g-bg-gray10 u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-large"><div class="c-siteReview_main g-inner-spacing-medium"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader c-siteReviewHeader-user u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium u-flexbox-alignCenter"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewScore"><a><div data-v-e408cafe="" class="c-siteReviewScore_background c-siteReviewScore_background-user"><div data-v-e408cafe="" title="User score 9 out of 10" aria-label="User score 9 out of 10" class="c-siteReviewScore u-flexbox-column u-flexbox-alignCenter u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-text-bold c-siteReviewScore_green c-siteReviewScore_user g-color-gray90 c-siteReviewScore_small"><span data-v-e408cafe="">9</span></div></div></a></div> <a href="/user/AdoMobA/" class="c-siteReviewHeader_username g-text-bold g-color-gray90 g-text-link u-text-underline-under" title="AdoMobA">
    AdoMobA
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Mar 16, 2023
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Pros
- fun open world with a bunch of mini souls levels to discover
- the Legacy dungeons feel distinct and properly intimidating
- the enemy variety is off the chart
- the weapon variety is staggering
- the game looks beautiful
- three games worth of content for a price of one

Cons
- repeating minibosses with the DS2 mentality of: But now there are two
- Mountaintops of Giants feel weirdly balanced compared to the rest of the game

Over ten years of work led to a masterpiece, where Fromsoft used everything they learned to make their biggest and baddest game yet. It would be criminal not to call this game a masterpiece, though a flawed one.

Elden Ring encompasses everything from the previous entries, the good and bad. Way more of the good though, like way, way more. Elden Ring expands on weapon skills from DS3 through Ashes of War. Most weapons are capable of slotting myriad of skills to fit any play style imaginable.

The points of interest on the map are divided into a couple of tiers of locations, signaling their quality. Legacy dungeons are massive sprawling levels where the most work has been put in. They have shortcuts that you can unlock with some diligent exploring and feature the main fights of the game.

Then there are major locations, like Castle Morne, Castle Sol, Caria Manor and a few others. Love and care was put into these locations, but they are nowhere near as expansive and twisted as the Legacy dungeons.

And then there are the minor locations. Caves, crypts, mines, you name it, this game has it. These places vary so heavily in quality it is never sure, if you are getting a banger, like a certain crypt with a Groundhog Day style puzzle, or if you are getting a complete dud with one of the games' many copy and pasted bosses.

Boss design in this game is about as wild in quality as the minor locations. Your main fights against the Shard Bearers are fun occasions that make your blood pump. Some of the minor bosses, especially Crucible Knights for me, put you through fun and challenging fights that will leave you smiling. And then there are the duds.

I swear to god, if I see another Tree Spirit in my life I will hurl. The first dragon fight is fun and exhilarating and fulfills the knight fantasy of charging a dragon on a horse fantastically. The twentieth dragon you fight has you sigh and get it over with. Whoever designed the first Royal Revenant should be fired. And the person that decided to copy and paste him twenty times over should never work in the industry again. Topping off these duds is the DS2 mindset of doubling the amount of bosses in the room and calling it done. The fight against the three Crystalians is the lowest point of this game for me.

After getting all that off my chest, Elden Ring shines on a second playthrough and on. Aka, once you know where the things you want are, you can just run for them and ignore everything you do not want to deal with.

More than ever, Elden Ring is the Fromsoft game where you dictate the difficulty, where in the older games you were forced to go one of three directions to continue, if you feel like the place that will continue the story is too big a hassle, you can just walk a random direction, gain a couple levels, get new tools to deal with it and then triumph.

So, Elden Ring. Fromsofts biggest game yet. A flawed masterpiece that deserves all the praise it got and more. By the way I talk about it you might think I hate this game. But no. Elden Ring is my game of 2022. It has given me so much to love and so much to think about for the last year, that I personally think it will stand the test of time as one of gaming's greatest achievements.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>So here it is! 11 years after a real "Masterpiece" Dark souls 1, 13 years after the foundation Demon Souls. If you like it or not, but these games were the foundation of a whole new genre and next generations of video games.

So, years of experience in the same base of genre must bring out something really new and improved, right?

The Play style - Dark Souls 3 with more anime weapon arts. Some Enemies and Bosses require a specific way to play.
Weapons - There are  over 300 weapons and 70 spells. How many do you need? How many of them are useful? How many do you test of the usefulness?
Animations, enemy and player models - every previous souls game (not bosses). And that's for real. Recycling at its finest.
Crafting - forgettable
Story -  forgettable. Very good idea, to bring to the Shakespearean cryptic story more of the same.
The chosen one going to kill or speak or interact with great ones like Miquella, Millicent, melina, miriel and rennala, renna, ranni and gowry, godwyn, godfry and morgott, mogh.
Remember Nito? Or Gwyn? Why do they make so much nonsense-people to forget about?
Then again, why should I care about the Story or Plot? The intro Scene is getting worse every Souls game, more cryptic and less care to make the plot interesting.
The open world - the Art style is more like High Fantasy. I expected to see elves and dwarves dancing around rainbows. And it didn't get better. No more Dark Fantasy than, I guess.
The open world itself is useless. I wouldn't call it empty, but it's more empty than previous titles.
It's boring to discover the same enemies in another color.
It's boring to ride around without a real destination. "But there is a destination, check the map!" Sure, but why do I need to have an open world then. Why not make smaller Areas with more detail. Even the "story areas" in this game have fewer details than the predecessor

I stop here. There are games (ubi-titles, cod, battlefield and so on) which got bashed because of the redundancy. Right so, I guess. But why not does anybody even mention it for the Souls games.

In this game there are the same negatives since demon souls: Camera ****, Hit boxes ****, all the same fighting styles (hit, block, dodge, cast spell) animations, graphically PS3, bad quest lines (if you miss a quest line or a NPC at the right time, your fault) and still nothing is shown or explained properly. I do not care if you are a hardcore fan, an option to turn tips on or off is not a negative thing and will nothing take away of the way you experience the game.
At least they worked on the very best part in every Soul's game: the platforming. Now there is a special jump button which make the char jump. And the horse. Super Mario at its best.

So, I had no fun playing this game. It was just too big and redundant and unimportant.
I still love playing Bloodborne somehow, even it has the same old flaws every souls game have

But If that's the future of gaming and a masterpiece, I am out.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>My first Souls type game. When I first got it I hated it cause it was stupidly hard. Wanted to instantly return it. Then I found out you can farm runes and make yourself a bit stronger. Seemed only fair since everything one shots you anyway. So I farmed a bit, got strong enough to the point where I wouldn't instantly die and had much more fun that way. I made the game fair for myself and loved every second of it after that. Now that I know how the game is I could probably play it without farming and still have fun since I know what I'd be getting myself into. The game is great, the world is great, it looks beautiful, and the combat is fun. Deciding between magic or physical is great. Play however you wanna play. Another platinum trophy on my account and I enjoyed getting it.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>"Will I enjoy this game if I beat the previous Souls games?"
Yes, but it will either land at the top of your FromSoft list or near the bottom.

-Elden Ring reads your inputs instead of deriving from self-contained enemy behavior.
-Elden Ring does not run well on PS4, even if you have a PS4 Pro with an SSD.
-Elden Ring has a mixed Souls OST, a good score for most IPs, but subpar Souls soundtrack.
-Elden Ring robs player agency, you will react to bosses like in Sekiro, but without a baked in parry system. The enemies do not abide by the rules the player has imposed on them, a stark difference between Bloodborne and Souls games.
-Elden Ring has the same flavor text writer that overexplains everything like in DS3. The writers for DeS and DS1 are apparently gone.

+Elden Ring has fixed most of the PvP balancing and is almost on par with DS3's*
+Elden Ring has dungeons, similar to Chalice Dungeons, but much less variety.
+Elden Ring has jumping.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>A mi parecer es la cúspide de los juegos de fromsoftware. Todo es excelente: el mundo abierto, el combate, el diseño de niveles, los jefes, los elementos rpg del juego, la dirección de arte, todo.

Si no les gustó el juego y nunca antes habían jugado un souls les recomiendo que le den otra oportunidad. Cuando yo jugué dark souls años atrás no me gustó la primera vez, el sistema de combate lo encontraba incomodo, estaba perdido en un mundo que no te decía a donde ir, y encontraba el juego injusto. Pero una vez que entiendes el sistema de combate, y logras pasar el primer filtro de dificultad, el juego te engancha de una manera increíble. El juego no es malo, solo es distinto a la mayoría de los juegos que uno suele estar acostumbrado a jugar, y sí, es difícil, pero rara vez injusto. Si mueres en algún momento del juego suele ser responsabilidad tuya, y no por un error de diseño.

Respecto a los problemas de bugs tengo entendido que ya fueron solucionados, así que no hay razón para que no puedan disfrutar de esta joya.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>It's hard to rate Elden Ring. For a "Souls-Veteran" (like me) it was definitely fun to play. But i can't agree with people calling this game "revolutionary" because it's simply wrong. Indeed compared with Dark Souls or other FromSoftware-titles it has an open world, a horse you can ride on and interesting additions like weapon-arts and ghost ashes. These Ashes are maybe the only new invetion Elden ring came up with. In my opinion the open world is way too big, and looks blunt at so many places. combat on horse isn't fun at all and dungeons like the most bosses are repetetive like hell. Seriously dungeons are the worst. Maybe 5 % of them are different to others and they all contain a boss we have already seen before somewhere. Anyway beside the justified critic (according to me) elden ring is a great game. It shines in common FromSoftware-strengthes: Character and monster design, beautifull environment (legacy dungeons like academia, stormveil castle or house volcano) and a great combat system with awesome bossfights. If you cut away 90 % of all dungeons (because they are all the same) and cut down the open world to a half i would defenitely say this is a masterpiece, otherwise it's a solid fun game with strengths and weaknesses. (8/10)</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Очередной забагованный шедевр от азиатского жулика. Все те же проблемы что и в Dark Souls 3 и прочих поделок этой команды бракоделов : пробой оружием сквозь стены/колонны, искусственно замедленные характеристики героя (боссы намного быстрее, что обрекает игрока на бессмысленный гринд рун (т.е. потерю времени)), а автовыбор цели писала самая тупая обезьяна в этой команде. Завидую играющим на ПК - они хотя бы не платят, а качают этот шедевр бесплатно с торрентов. Вообще удивительно - ну сделали вы хардкорную игру - сделайте хотя бы выбор уровня сложности - все нормальные люди играют для удовольствия, а не для того чтобы материться от очередного босса который выносит игрока с двух быстрых ударов, пробивая колонны, не обращая внимание на поднятый игроком щит и прочие баги которыми кишит игра. Те дурачки которые гоняют в эту игру с утра до ночи качая персонажа всё равно не покупают игру, а качают её с торрентов (это либо школота которой мама купила раз в году игру и они задрачивают её до дыр, либо прыщавые жирдяи работающие курьерами/сисадминами и для них единственная отрада - играть в "хардкорные" игры, дабы в их бестолковой жизни был какой-то смысл). Поставлю два балла за хорошую работу дизайнеров. Программная же часть - дерьмо, а тех кто расставлял характеристики боссам - пинками выгнать из вашей конторы. скорее бы уже пройти этот кошмар. Застрял на боссе "Микелла, черный клинок.". Выбрасывать игру в рынок с таким количеством багов - просто грабёж.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

    viroodiem
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Sep 1, 2022
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Definitely among the best and most polished "soulsborne" maso/core titles from FromSoft. There is just so much content to be had in this sandbox. Some of it is repetitive but no more than say Skyrim or Fallout.

The only real problem is there is a serious spike in difficulty when you enter end game areas. That does stand to reason but its not balanced with the game.

There are minor flaws like the need to play the game with a guide with how easy it is to break quest lines.

Some of the low level dungeon bosses are just plain terrible. Not difficult. Not imaginative.

The game has a high difficulty curve to start off with about till the point you get to Stormveil Castle. Then the game gets ridiculously easy through the middle until you start wrapping up content around the Capital city and spikes way further than it should and does not let up for the remainder of the game. Again, being a maso/core title you want an difficult ending but it should be within reason and not force you to have to rebuild your character in order to match a specific build. Thats one of From Softs biggest flaws in design. Forcing you to play a certain way even if its not technically required but the inflated difficulty leaves you little other option.

Another complaint is the clearly cut content and some of the dropped ideas. It also would have been nice to focus some development on archery from horseback which is practically impossible. Hopefully if there is an Elden Ring 2 it will add that cause with the addition of the horse that was a major oversight.

Also the quests could be a bit more intuitive. We dont want WoW/GTA holding your hand but we also dont want MYST level hands off either.

But all in all this is the most polished and closest to perfect offering we have gotten from FS. For all its flaws this is 2022s game of the year. Hands down.

A technical feat given how smoothly it plays on first generation PS4s. You wont find a deeper or more immersive game on PS4. If you dont sink at least 100/200 hours of your life into this world you are doing it wrong. I literally capped my play through at 999h 59m 59s and still have dozens of bosses to work through and content left to explore.

If you are capable of handing FromSoft type of games then there is no excuse for you to NOT have Elden Ring.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

    Hugus
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Aug 15, 2022
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>4/5
Creo que lo único que me impide ponerle un 5/5 a este juego es el endgame. Siento que la mayoria de las cosas en el endgame estan hechas para matarte de 2 golpes, incluso con vigo alto. Esto sirve para reflejar lo peligroso y poderosos que son algunos seres en este mundo, funciona especialmente bien con los semi dioses. Pero desde el punto de vista como jugador, por el gameplay, no es muy disfrutable tener peleas contra enemigos que tienen "ese ataque" que me acaban matando casi al comienzo de la pelea. No siempre hay un buen ritmo con estos jefes, no siento que haya una danza disfrutable en la pelea.

A pesar de todo, la variedad y libertad que ofrece este juego es inmensa. Cuando piensas que ya lo haz visto todo, siempre hay más por explorar, por enfrentar y contemplar. Amo la libertad que ofrece este juego, desde el mundo abierto hasta la personalización de tu personaje, poder cambiar de build en cualquiero momento es una gran oportunidad para jugadores que se topan con un bloqueo.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>FromSoftware doesn't miss.

Elden Ring is the culmination of everything FromSoftware has done in the last 10 years. From combat, exploration, boss fights, lore, everything. Playing this game felt like a love letter from FromSoftware.

The open world is the newest aspect this souls-like offers and it's done masterfully, there is a lot to explore and a lot to intrigue you to explore. However, this is also a fatal flaw of Elden Ring, as on subsequent playthroughs this allure for exploration is extinguished, as the excitement and wonder of discovering new places and dungeons is exclusive to your first playthrough (except of course of the areas you missed, which is probable).

I love that there is a myriad of builds you can try with the various weapons and spells.

This game doesn't necessarily feel like a pioneer in its genre, but a statement of everything that has come before in its genre, both the good and the bad, but 95% of the time the good.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

    Cloud9846
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>This game is for the NES/Famicom generation.  Those of us that grew up on Dragon Warrior, Ghosts and Goblins, Megaman, and especially ZELDA 1 AND 2 will wholeheartedly appreciate this experience.  This game is essentially Zelda 2 and Castlevania 2 packaged in a neat little bow for 2022.  Yes, it is a masterpiece.</span></div> <!----> <!----></div></div> <div class="c-siteReview_extra u-grid u-grid-gap-medium g-inner-spacing-medium o-border-thin-top g-border-gray30 c-siteReview_extra-user"><!----> <div class="c-siteReview_externalLink g-color-gray80 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter c-siteReview_flag"><svg class="g-outer-spacing-right-small"><use xlink:href="#flag"></use></svg> <span class="g-text-link u-text-underline-under u-text-uppercase">Report</span></div> <!----> <div class="c-siteReview_platform g-text-bold g-color-gray80 g-text-xsmall u-text-right u-text-uppercase">
      PlayStation 4
    </div></div></div> <!----> <!----></div><div><div class="c-siteReview g-bg-gray10 u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-large"><div class="c-siteReview_main g-inner-spacing-medium"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader c-siteReviewHeader-user u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium u-flexbox-alignCenter"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewScore"><a><div data-v-e408cafe="" class="c-siteReviewScore_background c-siteReviewScore_background-user"><div data-v-e408cafe="" title="User score 9 out of 10" aria-label="User score 9 out of 10" class="c-siteReviewScore u-flexbox-column u-flexbox-alignCenter u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-text-bold c-siteReviewScore_green c-siteReviewScore_user g-color-gray90 c-siteReviewScore_small"><span data-v-e408cafe="">9</span></div></div></a></div> <a href="/user/Wrath_4givnez/" class="c-siteReviewHeader_username g-text-bold g-color-gray90 g-text-link u-text-underline-under" title="Wrath_4givnez">
    Wrath_4givnez
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Jun 7, 2022
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Been a while since I visited this site, but I wanted to talk about this game.

FromSoft's latest masterpiece doesn't really need very much introduction, especially since it had become THE most popular game in the "SoulsBorne" series of games that they've produced. Everyone knows (and probably expects) that it's a challenging, yet rewarding, experience that will last from when you first pick up the controller to the final time you put it down (which could very will be a long time away). You will explore, fight, die, and triumph over the odds, meeting interesting (and sometimes shady) characters that have their own agendas that may go with or against your own, as you have previously in other games under FromSoft's banner.

However, what sets this apart from other games in the series is the big genre addition it was given; Open-World. While previous titles did have exploration as part of the ethos (as finding gear and items will GREATLY increase your chances of survival), the games have always been structured as mostly semi-linear designs (with Demon's Souls being the closest to a linear style game). Many of them have been described to be akin to a Metroidvania (which I've recently began to disagree with, due to the many points of no return without teleporting), but it's very clear that despite the large area a player could see across the horizon, said player would likely only be able to explore a portion of it, with the rest being entirely out of bounds/blocked off/impossible to get to. General locations obviously could be seen and later explored, but restrictions are still placed that aren't immediately noticed (due to how well those games were structured, masking the linearity of the design).

Elden Ring, however, removes those borders. If you can see it, be a general location or a specific one, you can go there. The only borders that ever seem to be present are shore-lines at coasts around the country sides. The vast lakes, plains, mountains, valleys, beaches, hills, and plateaus that once served as background dressing that the player would only ever set foot on for a fraction of what was shown is now entirely open, explorable, and populated with a variety of creatures, items, materials, and points of interest, all of which are rarely shown on the map until you've physically come across it or **** it down yourself. Even repeated sites, such as shacks, caves, crypts, ruins, or camps almost always feel different with different enemies, set ups, items, and significance to your journey. You'll never run into a location in this game and deal with it the exact same way, unlike most other open world games. Furthermore, due to how the game-world is structured, it's no longer impossible to be entirely stuck when hitting a "brick wall" (a challenge too high compared to your skills/stats), because now you can just... go literally any other direction, and find something else to do. That said, this also comes at the cost of meandering quite a bit around the vast landscapes of the "Lands Between", sometimes getting lost in over-leveled areas, or even indulging too much on exploration and resource gathering that you end up overpowering yourself and steam-rolling over anything in your path, which all can create a wildly inconsistent difficulty structure. Then again, because of the way it's built, it just means it really is up to you on how far and how often you want to go off the beaten path, how much you want to avoid progressing the story, and how much you want to challenge/unchallenge yourself.

Personally, it's one of my absolute favorite things about the game. I haven't felt this joyful, cautious, terrified, curious, anxious, awestruck, or anything else in between in an open world type game in a long time, entirely satisfying my desire to explore every nook and cranny I can find, no matter how mundane.

This isn't to say they've done away with the tight, inter-connectivity they had in previous games. Major points of interest (for example; Stormveil Castle), and smaller dungeons such as caves and crypts, are still very tightly and deliberately designed in the same style any SoulsBorne vet would be used to; semi-linear, interwoven and interconnected corridors and rooms, with secrets and alternate paths very carefully placed, with an attention to give hints to the player on how to get somewhere without any hand=holding.

Honestly, the only real major criticism I could give the game would have to be the heavy pop-in after you respawn/teleport to a resting place, as well as the frame-rate stutter when there's too much going on at once (seems to be less present in the PS5 version, but I'm not 100% sure on that). However, it doesn't quite detract from the gameplay, and the over all look of the game, even when just journeying from one end of the massive world map to the other, is absolutely incredible.

It will be a long time before I let this game lay down to rest. Happy Hunting, potential Elden Lords.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Note: I believe all the bad reviews are either they are newcomer to souls series or its another fans or even developers from another game that have or will release their game this year. Elden Ring is not a type of game that you can understand or appreciate if you come from action, hack &amp; slash or simply looking for "relaxing" and "fun" game. Elden Ring has its own definition of fun and you need to keep playing it to understand their game design.

GOTY of 2022 for sure, but I'll still pick Sekiro over Elden Ring.

Elden Ring is the first game I've ever pre-ordered due to expectation to see more of Sekiro in the game but turns out its more into Dark Souls style.

Don't get me wrong, Although i hate Dark Souls but this game is very great! Its the most pleasing exploration game I've ever played. Many things to discovered and room to improve your character as well as variation to improve it.

It still bring the gene of FromSoftware as they are the best at creating the best rewarding game. I can feel I've achieved or obtain something in every moment I play this game which not easy to accomplish in gaming nowadays.

The world design is fascinating and surprisingly the world of Elden Ring is way too massive but surely not empty like in other open world game. Although, the world is filled with dangerous in every corner so the feel of getting cautious is always there.

The reason I'll still pick Sekiro over Elden Ring is due to its combat system and story. Sekiro is fast-paced where Elden Ring is kinda slow and the combat is Sekiro is very fluid with animation of finishing kill to complement that. Beating the boss in Sekiro feels like an achievement while in Elden Ring most of it only the matter of you overpowering the boss (well, not all of them). In Sekiro you are cautiously aggressive while in Elden Ring is more aggressively cautious.

Just hope FromSoftware could come with another Sekiro game.

Other than that, FromSoftware successfully create a rich and meaningful open world in their 1st attempt with more understandable story this time around. On my 2nd play-through now as I keep killing every NPC that I met on my 1st run --"</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Reluctant about the possibility of poor performance on the PS4 base system I just couldn't resist in the end and I'm glad I did pick it up anyway. The game for me is a brilliant piece of work. It plays like a SoulsBorne game and is relentless because you might just venture in areas you shouldn't ben at or there might be strong foes in easier areas where you didn't expect them. In the graphics department the 'legacy dungeons' feel more detailed than the open world but considering the PS4's old age it's no surprise. I'm 25 hours in so I've probably barely touched the surface yet this game is making me want to get back to the game... just a few more minutes just to realize a few hours have passed again; it's just so satisfying. Not all good news though, for me the major drawbacks are the crafting system which feels like a bad designed idea. 'Lets gather ingredients and craft items you just looted in the world during dark souls/bloodborne play throughs)', another issue for me is the side-quest tracking.   </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>i really like this game and want to play but i can't. Because the game for Asia version doesn't support English in-game and i don't know any Chinese or Korean.</span></div> <!----> <!----></div></div> <div class="c-siteReview_extra u-grid u-grid-gap-medium g-inner-spacing-medium o-border-thin-top g-border-gray30 c-siteReview_extra-user"><!----> <div class="c-siteReview_externalLink g-color-gray80 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter c-siteReview_flag"><svg class="g-outer-spacing-right-small"><use xlink:href="#flag"></use></svg> <span class="g-text-link u-text-underline-under u-text-uppercase">Report</span></div> <!----> <div class="c-siteReview_platform g-text-bold g-color-gray80 g-text-xsmall u-text-right u-text-uppercase">
      PlayStation 4
    </div></div></div> <!----> <!----></div><div><div class="c-siteReview g-bg-gray10 u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-large"><div class="c-siteReview_main g-inner-spacing-medium"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader c-siteReviewHeader-user u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium u-flexbox-alignCenter"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewScore"><a><div data-v-e408cafe="" class="c-siteReviewScore_background c-siteReviewScore_background-user"><div data-v-e408cafe="" title="User score 8 out of 10" aria-label="User score 8 out of 10" class="c-siteReviewScore u-flexbox-column u-flexbox-alignCenter u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-text-bold c-siteReviewScore_green c-siteReviewScore_user g-color-gray90 c-siteReviewScore_small"><span data-v-e408cafe="">8</span></div></div></a></div> <a href="/user/kirrwed/" class="c-siteReviewHeader_username g-text-bold g-color-gray90 g-text-link u-text-underline-under" title="kirrwed">
    kirrwed
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Apr 23, 2022
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Elden Ring is a well-polished open-world adventure. Much of it is customizable to player preferences. From character design to which way to explore first, and more. The weapons and armaments are many. The game encourages various builds in concert with fight styles, from melee, to range, to a mix.

The game is known for difficulty, yet—despite the tendency of some to confuse difficulty with excellence—it offers the player a couple different ways to succeed. The first is obviously to develop skill, and for many players, this means much trial and error, learning boss patterns, and eventually finding a rhythm by which to win. A second method includes some of the first but also includes levelling-up before returning to a difficult boss or area. This is a great option that make it open to a larger variety of skill levels without flipping an “easy” switch per se.

Much of the visuals, environments, and boss appearances are intricate and cinematic. Exploration is encouraged and rewarding, finding new places, new save points, new caves, new powerups, etc. The game does well to follow the 30-second rule of filling its world with enough intrigue to never really get boring. The exploration and variety of NPCs, quests, powerups, places, etc. is the strength of this game. The experience is largely driven by where the player wants to go, with a main questline available at all times.

Despite all the adventurous and customizable positives in this game, it is far from perfect, despite such reviews.

What makes many of the boss fights difficult is a “one hit kill” move. A player may often methodically maneuver through a fight for several minutes and then fall to an “instant kill” only to lose all that time and effort for what amounts to a “cheap” move that often can only be anticipated by trial and error. Sometimes, the blow might come so out of nowhere, you won’t even know why you died, such as with the second phase of the Radahn fight if you happened to have the camera in the wrong direction during a mid-fight breather. Most fights have minimal cerebral solutions. Many don’t feel like they beat you in an even fight. They only beat you because of a knockout punch, including ones that put you (or your horse) in stunlock to then finish you with additional follow-ups. At the end of the day, “pattern” based bosses with the “one-hit” are rather cheap designs. It’s almost an illusion of difficulty, where a fight seems somewhat fair and a good rumble until they get in the “cheap shot” and that’s often the only thing that consistenly makes them difficult.

Also, too many games, including Elden Ring, create difficulty in part by forbidding “cancellation” of a move. Part of the game’s challenge is anticipating your melee or magic “wind up” time and delivery. This can last up to several seconds. It leaves your character vulnerable if hit meanwhile. And you can’t cancel out of it if you, the player, actually sees the interruption in time and has the reflexes to cancel. The controller will actually be impotent until the animation is complete. This mechanic doesn’t feel natural, as a real person would be able to cancel their own punch.

Another feature in some boss fights that is poor is the bosses that have a second phase that is independent from the first phase’s HP meter. Unless you want to scout out a fight by watching spoiler videos, there is no way to know how much pacing of resources you want to use in a given fight because most of the time, the HP meter you see represents the opponent’s total HP, not some surprise new “refilled” HP bar from a second phase. Things like this just make gameplay aggravating and unfun.

There are many consumable items, like greases or crab meat, that can be crafted or purchased and used as buffs. These last for a period of time. However, if you are killed, these are lost forever. They are not like runes you can at least have a chance to recover after you are killed. It made 1-time use items overly precious. Your inventory doesn’t return to what it was before a fight or last save. And with so many of the fights being trial and error, it’s very easy to burn through many such items for naught. Few tutorials seem to utilize these, either. The game simply doesn’t encourage them because of it’s loyalty to difficulty and unforgiving gameplay.

As a side note, the game creates a fictional world of peculiar, amorality. It helps to be a spiritually knowledgable or careful person when playing the game. Because in Elden Ring, it seems the lines between good and evil are often quite blurred, to the point where NPCs ask strangely worded things like “will you serve the witch?” which in base reality would be clearly unwise to assuage. But the game seems to blur or alter the meaning of things like witches, blasphemy, and other spiritual terms, while yet insisting on borrowing from traditional spiritual language.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">
        Read More

    Apr 13, 2022
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Elden Ring is a truly great game and a definite contender for Game of the Year, and probably the favorite to win the award at this point in the year.

My biggest negative of the game is the change in music the game uses. In other From Soft games there is no music while you're exploring, just your footsteps and the sounds of monsters and combat, and then when the music kicks it, so does the dread and realization that you're about to get your butt kicked. The music in older games sticks out more because of this and becomes more memorable. Other negatives are slight balance issues, performance issues regarding frame rates (dying to due to frame rate drops in a boss fight can be quite frustrating), and hit box/hit registration; while hit boxes are in general better compared to older games, the open world aspect can lead to environments really messing up hit boxes and hit registration.

Despite these flaws, I'm giving this game a 10/10 due to everything it does so right and so well. The best boss designs in the game are absolute *chef's kiss* and jaw dropping. The environment diversity is gorgeous and original. There is a massive amount of weapons, spells, incantations, weapon arts, et cetera, and just so many ways to play the game with all the different items and such. There is so much fantastic content in this game; where certain game companies (*cough* Ubisoft *cough*), From Soft has filled this game with boss fight after boss fight after boss fight, and then all the weapons, armor, spells, etc. that I mentioned before. Aesthetic is what From Soft does best, and Elden Ring oozes style and creativity like an open wound oozes blood. The game is just beautiful.

While the game is not perfect, it is still an absolute masterpiece, and I cannot wait to put hundreds of more hours in as I create more characters, play new builds, and experience as much as possible. Git gud, and don't you dare go hollow!</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

      PlayStation 4
    </div></div></div> <!----> <!----></div><div><div class="c-siteReview g-bg-gray10 u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-large"><div class="c-siteReview_main g-inner-spacing-medium"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader c-siteReviewHeader-user u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium u-flexbox-alignCenter"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewScore"><a><div data-v-e408cafe="" class="c-siteReviewScore_background c-siteReviewScore_background-user"><div data-v-e408cafe="" title="User score 7 out of 10" aria-label="User score 7 out of 10" class="c-siteReviewScore u-flexbox-column u-flexbox-alignCenter u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-text-bold c-siteReviewScore_yellow c-siteReviewScore_user g-color-gray90 c-siteReviewScore_small"><span data-v-e408cafe="">7</span></div></div></a></div> <a href="/user/blakfayt/" class="c-siteReviewHeader_username g-text-bold g-color-gray90 g-text-link u-text-underline-under" title="blakfayt">
    blakfayt
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Mar 30, 2022
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Game starts off really strong. Like, the first 30-40 hours, depending on how much exploring you do, are the most incredible feeling. But by the time you're reaching the end of a normal Souls game, 50-60 hours, the cracks start to appear. I'm at 70 hours, I just got past the royal capital, and I'm beating bosses in 1 try with multiple healing items left over. Bosses I've never seen before are doing LESS DAMAGE THAN NORMAL ENEMIES. This game feels like FromSoft inverted the damage, making bosses a joke and mooks a chore. I'm walking by hordes of foes chasing after me with everything they have because they take too long to kill, are too dangerous to engage, and at level 112 I know I can beat a boss in one try if I have all my flasks. It's not about the game being too easy or too hard, it's just plain unbalanced.

Strength builds can barely get a hit out without trading, which can lead to you taking 40% of your life to deal 10% of the boss' life. Dex builds deal 1/20th of the boss' life, and rarely have the opening to swing more than once because the bosses swing 20 times in a row, do an AoE body explosion, and then do another combo that lasts a half an hour. Magic builds are flat out OP, even more than usual because of the open world allowing them to find all their gear right from the start and then start steam rolling bosses with non-boss spells.

Elden Ring isn't a bad game, but FromSoft needs to do more than nerf play abilities to balance this game. The bosses need a second look, because I probably shouldn't beat Rahdan, Morgott, Astell, and Renalla in one try, but exploring the royal capital is like pulling my teeth out because of instant death curses in the sewers and knights stunlocking me with lightning damage in the streets. Balance.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

Sin embargo, al jugar la version final me quedo tranquilo al ver que solucionaron los defectos.
He jugado a casi todos los juegos de la saga Soulsbornekiro asi que ya sabia que esperar de un juego de from software.
Siento que el juego esta bastante bien equilibrado en cuanto a dificultad y curva de aprendizaje. Hay que saber como jugarlo.
Se debe explorar el mundo abierto tanto para encontrar elementos de mejora, armas interesantes y poder subir de nivel.
Teniendo experiencia en juegos como Skyrim y Fallout, supe adaptarme muy bien a la mecanica de mundo abierto, la cual disfruto mucho.
En cuanto al combate, cada build tiene lo suyo asi que cada uno debe adaptarse a su propio estilo de juego. Refiriendonos a la historia, el lore y NPC son bastante interesantes.
El combate a caballo agrega una nueva experiencia de la que eres completamente libre de usar o no usar.

    Gabechill
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Mar 19, 2022
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Technical issues can be fixed, so I'm rating the game based on content only.
The world is huge and beautiful but there is a LOT of empty space.
The battles bring nothing new to the table, you basically do the same thing you have been doing in every Souls game: roll and dodge the enemy's attack, roll at the wrong time and the enemy hits you, run to be at a safe distance from the enemy to be able to heal and approach the enemy once again and hit it a couple of times. Everything feels heavy and clunky and your hundreds of deaths feel somehow even more frustrating than in any Souls game. Sekiro's combat is way better, more dynamic, more visceral and more engaging. I was really hoping that Elden Ring would improve on Sekiro's combat and take it from there, but we just got the old and recycled Souls' stiff, clunky mechanics that, by now, feel stale. The rewards for killing the most tough bosses were useless most of the time: summons that I wouldn't bother trying, underwhelming talismans, average weapons that I didn't even bothered selling for their low price and other trinkets I couldn't care less about. The lore felt too vague for my taste. I know that's FS's style, but I was really expecting a big, revealing, plot-twisting ending, because my 100-hour journey was arduous and I thought I deserved a decent ending. No, the ending was short, vague and underwhelming, to the point I felt it was disrespectful. All is left for me now is hope that in From's next title, I can be immersed into a huge and beautiful world with a slightly more fathomable lore, an overwhelming, big, fulfilling ending and improved and innovative combat. The old FS's formula still might be appealing to die-hard fans, but I don't think it's going to survive much longer.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Elden Ring is about every bit as fantastic as most of FromSoftware's other Soulslike titles. The biggest difference now is that there's a huge open world to freely explore, but it's just one of many changes. There's of course the new horse gameplay and combat which is very fun, new ways to craft recipes and add signature abilities to weapons, a counter attack move which is incredibly useful for shield builds, and a lot of accessability such as control mapping. Similar to the rest of the Souls library, the game does share the same frustrating quirks like still getting hit through solid walls and the occasional bug or framerate drop (at least on last-gen platforms), but that's all outshined by the incredible presentation of the Lands Between, a place filled with so much mystery it's hard resisting the urge to discover and conquor everything there is to see.   </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>I played every From title since Demon's Souls on PS3, when it was still an obscure game found in the back of some retailer's shelves.
I loved all of them, they always were beautiful, inspired, and challenging. But fair.
Elden Ring is by far the most beautiful; visually stunning and with one of the best maps ever created, you just can't stop exploring.
But.
There's a huge But.
It crossed the line which separates a challenging, yet fun, game, from a painful and frustrating experience.
After 105 hours I'm sick of being stunlocked by everything, from floor damage to arrows, even when wearing a Scale Armor.
I'm sick that every type of enemy, even dragons, keep jumping around like ninjas.
I'm sick of the near-infinite enemy combos that end up with a dodge or backstep /repeat.
I'm sick of the constant need of using an overall artificial difficulty which is nowhere near to the concept of Fun.
Yes, Elden Ring is where From games stopped being fun.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">
        Read More
      </span> <!----> <!----></button></div> <!----></div></div> <div class="c-siteReview_extra u-grid u-grid-gap-medium g-inner-spacing-medium o-border-thin-top g-border-gray30 c-siteReview_extra-user"><!----> <div class="c-siteReview_externalLink g-color-gray80 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter c-siteReview_flag"><svg class="g-outer-spacing-right-small"><use xlink:href="#flag"></use></svg> <span class="g-text-link u-text-underline-under u-text-uppercase">Report</span></div> <!----> <div class="c-siteReview_platform g-text-bold g-color-gray80 g-text-xsmall u-text-right u-text-uppercase">

      PlayStation 4
    </div></div></div> <!----> <!----></div><div><div class="c-siteReview g-bg-gray10 u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-large"><div class="c-siteReview_main g-inner-spacing-medium"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader c-siteReviewHeader-user u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium u-flexbox-alignCenter"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewScore"><a><div data-v-e408cafe="" class="c-siteReviewScore_background c-siteReviewScore_background-user"><div data-v-e408cafe="" title="User score 8 out of 10" aria-label="User score 8 out of 10" class="c-siteReviewScore u-flexbox-column u-flexbox-alignCenter u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-text-bold c-siteReviewScore_green c-siteReviewScore_user g-color-gray90 c-siteReviewScore_small"><span data-v-e408cafe="">8</span></div></div></a></div> <a href="/user/Scendence/" class="c-siteReviewHeader_username g-text-bold g-color-gray90 g-text-link u-text-underline-under" title="Scendence">
    Scendence
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Mar 10, 2022
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>After 50 hours of playtime and beating every main boss, I can say the game is amazing. It still has it's issues, but the overall experience is one of the best I've ever had while playing a game. I played on a launch day PS4 and doing so led to a few points where the frames dropped to almost a standstill. This only happened a few times, but it's one of the reasons holding the game back from a 9 or 10. I guarantee that if I were to play this on a PS5 or RTX 3000+, the game would be near perfect.

The map is massive and has something to do no matter where you go. The only thing is, rather than telling you where to go or giving you a waypoint to follow, you have to find everything yourself. The game doesn't hold your hand in any aspect of the game including the map. You have to pay attention to near every piece of dialogue in order to pick up clues that will hint to where you need to go next.

The combat is the culmination that everything FromSoft has work on in the last decade and you can clearly tell. Shades of DS3, Bloodborne, and Sekiro are all over this game. The bosses are very difficult, but not unfair or impossible. Margit is the toughest first story boss in the series, but there are multiple ways of going about the fight. One, you can keep trying over and over. Two, you can get stronger and come back later. Or three, find an item that might help with the boss. Margit's Shackle is an item the specifically helps with this boss. Every boss provides a unique challenge and forces you to come up with unconventional solutions. One of the biggest questions the game asks you is "Oh so you beat that boss? What if there were two of them?" Gank bosses are very common here and some aren't very well designed.

Like most Fromsoft stories, it's very vague and up to the player whether or not they really want to pay attention to it. This comes in the form of exploration. The more exploring you do, npc's you meet, and areas you unlock, the more the story starts to come together and give you the completed story. The story is as deep and fleshed out as the player is willing to make it.

Overall the game is around a High 8 to low 9 for me. First game in a long time that makes me want to get 100% in. If you are on the edge of buying it or not, try it out and see what happens, you might just find one of your favorite games of all time.

***SPOILERS***
There are still bosses that are poorly designed. Crucible knight and misbegotten warrior is painful to play against because the developers just threw two bosses in one fight without thinking about balance or the arena they fight you in. Godskin Duo is annoying because they tried to break agro by giving you pillars to hide behind, but it doesn't matter if both mobs are the same speed and both have ranged attacks. They tried to channel the spirit of O&amp;S, but fell short. Rykard is a reskinned version of Yhorm in the way that you need a special weapon that's specifically designed for the fight in order to have a chance at winning. The elden beast is probably my least favorite boss in the game. The fact that it has so many two-shot long ranged attacks is already hard, but it constantly runs to the other side of the stage a few seconds after you close the gap makes it 100x more annoying to fight.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

I went into the game and took my time, enjoyed the map and the countless hidden places and things in every corner of which there is many! I am still not 100% complete and have lots to do. Replayability is great offering so many different ways to go through the game to keep it new.
The only thing I found overtly difficult was the steep learning curve at the beginning, but don't let that dampen the brilliance of the rest of the game. You will catch on and any subsequent playthroughs will be even easier! This has made me realize how many games just let you be OP and walk through things.
Solid 9/10+

    Lord_of_ZXC
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Mar 8, 2022
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Итак, ознакомился с данным шедевром от Миядзаки сана на ps4 pro. И начну пожалуй с минусов. Не лучшая оптимизация. Из критических багов встретил только зависания в деревьях при прыжке с лошади и последующая смерть персонажа. Фреймрейт в целом приемлемый, хотя просадки есть, они, как и положено, раздражают, но в целом это не так критично. О графике трудно судить ввиду устаревшей консоли, но если говорить о картинке в целом, то она целостная. Ну и конечно же художники постарались на славу, да это не такой целостный мир, как например дс1. Но и масштабы этих миров сравнивать не очень приемлемо, как по мне. Далее о геймплее, некоторое оружие поломано. Из того что я встретил это катана реки крови, которая у меня не получила бонусов урона от скейлов и двуручник гатса, который при улучшении на +25 и закалке на тяжесть выдаёт меньше урона чем при улучшении на +24 и той же закалке, при чем меньше как базового урона, так и урона от скейла(с другими закалками такой проблемы нет). Теперь о хорошем. 65 часов, выбита платина и игра абсолютно не надоела. Боссы, исследование, чувство первооткрывателя, всё это отлично работает, особенно последнее, в силу специфики открытого мира. Играть круто и интересно, билдостроение пестрит новыми красками не забывая об истоках. Прокачаны анимации и касты многих заклинаний(в сравнении с предыдущими играми автора). Нпц и лор, в целом похожи на тот же дарк, примерная концепция та же, но есть больше дворцовых интриг, что наверняка пошло от сооавтора истории Дж. Мартина,но в целом это новый лор, новыми персонажами и событиями, опять же, схожи именно концепция, а не история. Подводя итог, лично мне как любителю серии, игра зашла абсолютно, всё чего я ожидал от игры оправдал себя. Отсылки на берсерка, мрачная, неоднозначная история, упадок мира, неочевидные квесты и конечно же крутые боссы. Смело могу заявить что лучший dark souls это  elden ring. А бал минусанул за повторяющихся мини-боссов и самую лёгкую платину в соулсборн серии Миядзаки</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Some occasional frame drops? ZERO OUT OF TEN!

Are you people serious? The rest of the game is an absolute triumph of art and design, as well as a culmination of most of the best mechanics from From Soft's game library, but you'll trash it for stuttering every once in a while? What a bunch of babies.

The problem with Cyberpunk 2077 at launch wasn't just that it had a bad framerate. The problem was that it would crash all the time, the AI was atrocious, entire features felt missing, and characters would just spawn in random locations sometimes. Elden Ring hasn't crashed for me once, the enemy AI are quite sophisticated, the game is packed to the brim with great content, and mechanically, everything seems really solid. And the performance hitches will probably be improved with patches over time.

Do these people not remember Blighttown? Would they also give the original Dark Souls a 0/10 because of its occasional hitches? Or Bloodborne, which is locked at 30 FPS for the entire game? Is that a 0/10? Or Skyrim, which still has tons of bugs TO THIS DAY? Definitely a 0/10.

None of these reviews are serious.

The game is not perfect, and I can absolutely understand docking a few points for performance hitches or language limitations if those things matter to you. Maybe a 7/10 or a 6/10, or heck, even a 3/10 if those things really, really matter to you. But a 0/10 for a game that is so clearly not garbage is not a useful review to anyone. It's just useless spite from people who want to feel smart for not liking a popular thing.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">

      PlayStation 4
    </div></div></div> <!----> <!----></div><div><div class="c-siteReview g-bg-gray10 u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-large"><div class="c-siteReview_main g-inner-spacing-medium"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader c-siteReviewHeader-user u-grid g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium u-flexbox-alignCenter"><div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewScore"><a><div data-v-e408cafe="" class="c-siteReviewScore_background c-siteReviewScore_background-user"><div data-v-e408cafe="" title="User score 9 out of 10" aria-label="User score 9 out of 10" class="c-siteReviewScore u-flexbox-column u-flexbox-alignCenter u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-text-bold c-siteReviewScore_green c-siteReviewScore_user g-color-gray90 c-siteReviewScore_small"><span data-v-e408cafe="">9</span></div></div></a></div> <a href="/user/Unholystorm/" class="c-siteReviewHeader_username g-text-bold g-color-gray90 g-text-link u-text-underline-under" title="Unholystorm">
    Unholystorm
  </a> <div class="c-siteReviewHeader_reviewDate g-color-gray80 u-text-uppercase">
    Mar 6, 2022
  </div></div> <div><div class="c-siteReview_quote g-outer-spacing-bottom-medium"><span>Excellent jeu.

Évidemment, Elden Ring à un style de gameplay qui peut en faire abandonner plusieurs. Par contre, il s'agit, comme pour tout les autres "souls games", d'un jeu mettant au défis notre état d'esprit, notre mindset.

Points forts:
-D'abord, le jeu donne une très grande liberté au joueur. Cela lui permet d'être créatif.
-L'open world rend le jeu beaucoup plus immersif que ses prédécesseurs.
-Le niveau de difficulté est sincèrement varié. Certains nous semblent impossible et d'autres seront tués du premier coup.
-Elden Ring à gardé son approche de type Dark souls. (C'est ce que les adeptes veulent)
-Le décor est varié et remplit de mystère et de nouveauté.
-La jouabilité est resté un élément important pour Myazaki. L'avatar est facile à utiliser.
-Les boss sont imprésionnant et amusant à faire. Même s'ils nous tue à répétition. Nous avons l'impression d'avoir la stratégie idéale au bout des doigts, ce qui rend le joueur plus confiant et donc plus persévérant.
-La grande quantité de site of grace. Le jeu nous fais un cadeau et place des statuts ou des site de grâce près des boss. Ce qui rend la "pratique" plus plaisante.
-Une série de nouveaux sorts et attaques puissantes. Fort bien.
-La musique de boss est très bonne. Dès l'ouverture du jeu, j'ai pris le temps d'écouter l'œuvre musical du menu. Cela met le ton du jeu. On ressent déjà sa tristesse, mais aussi la nécessité d'être courageux. Comme si l'un nourrissait l'autre.
-Torrent, notre monture est un beau cadeau en monde ouvert. Il est aussi utile en combat et rend le jeu plus facile, et ce, significativement. Par contre, il ne peut pas être utilisé contre certains boss ne faisant pas partie de la zone ouverte du jeu. Excellent pour l'exploration.
-Les sous-terrain sont aussi des mondes cartographiés.
-L'adition des esprits (spirits) est très bien. Utile pour faire distraction et sera plutôt apprécié par les nouveau joueur qui auront besoin de répits lors des gros combats.
-L'histoire reste énigmatique, mais cela fait partie du style de Myazaki. Toutefois, elle est plus claire dans Elden Ring que dans ses prédécesseurs.
-Avoir à d'découvrir les cartes cachés est plaisant.
-L'approche punitive aux erreurs et gratifiante aux réussites : Comme tous les souls games, le jeu invite le joueur à être persévérant. Réussir les boss demandera de l'observation, l'élaboration d'une stratégie (qui s'améliore à chaque expérience) et de comprendre comment "l'ordinateur" est programmer. Certaines attaque sont des algorithme précis dans certaines situation. Ce qui offre une ouverture certaines aux joueurs pour ne pas être punie et, profiter d'une frappe.

Points faible:
-La musique de la zone ouverte est bien, mais aurait pu être mieux.
-Personnellement, j'ai faire le jeu en solo pour le défis. Par contre, ce qui serait plaisant, c'est d'avoir un "multiplayer" ou "coop" mieux élaborer. Plus libre et moins restraignant. Quite à ne pas permettre les trophées.</span></div> <div class="c-globalButton g-outer-spacing-top-small c-globalButton-small c-globalButton-primary"><button class="c-globalButton_container g-text-normal g-height-100 u-flexbox u-flexbox-alignCenter u-pointer u-flexbox-justifyCenter g-width-fit-content"><span class="c-globalButton_label">
